Three Additional Types of Intellect
Enumerates three special types of intellect above the common intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of intellect beyond innate intellect: the gifted intellect, the ascetic intellect, and the honorable intellect of the Prophet.

Core Idea
Intellect is not one thing—it has special forms given by Allah.

The author, in his classification of intellect, moves beyond the basic division to identify three elevated types. These are not acquired through effort but are divinely bestowed or linked to spiritual states. This passage names and describes them briefly.

Guided Path
1
Read the three types
Read the Arabic list of three types: العقل العطائي، عقل الزهاد، العقل الشرفي. Notice how each is defined by its source or effect.
2
Understand 'Ata'i intellect
The first is 'Ata'i (gifted), given by Allah to believers to guide them to faith. It is a direct gift, not earned.
3
Understand ascetic intellect
The second is the intellect of the ascetics (zuhhad), which enables zuhd (renunciation). It is connected to piety.
4
Understand honorable intellect
The third is the honorable intellect, specific to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), because it is the most noble.
5
Reflect on the pattern
Notice that these three are not about reasoning but about gifts from Allah and spiritual attainments. They show that intellect can have different spiritual dimensions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث : عطائي ؛ وهو ما يعطيه الله للمؤمن ؛ ليهتدوا به إلى الإيمان.
والرابع: عقل الزهاد؛ وهو الذي يكون به الزهد.
والخامس شرفيّ ؛ وهو عقل نبينا ال؛ لأنه أشرف العقول .
وقد اختلف في تفضيل العقل على العلم أو العكس، والراجح تفضيل العلم على العقل؛ لأن العلم من صفاته تعالى وما يُروى في تفضيل العقل فهو موضوع لا أصل له ، كما صرح به الجلال السيوطي.
قوله : ولَكِنْ قَرَّرُوا فِيْهِ خِلَافاً أي لكن قرر العلماء في العقل خلافاً، ولا محل لهذا الاستدراك ؛ لأنهم قرروا في الروح خلافاً أيضاً، فلعل (لكن) لمجرد التأكيد، ثم رأيت المصنف في شرحه) قال: (ولكن ... إلى آخره) استدراك على طريقة الخائضين، فأشار إلى أنهم لم يتفقوا (۱) على حقيقةٍ معينةٍ، بل اختلفوا في بيانها (٢) . انتهى . فالاستدراك يُشعر بانتشار الخلاف وكثرته .
And the third: 'Ata'i (gifted); it is what God gives to the believer so that they may be guided by it to faith. And the fourth: the intellect of the ascetics; it is that by which asceticism occurs. And the fifth: honorable; it is the intellect of our Prophet (peace be upon him) because it is the most honorable of intellects. And there is disagreement concerning preferring intellect over knowledge or the opposite, and the preponderant view is the preference of knowledge over intellect, because knowledge is among His attributes, and what is narrated concerning the preference of intellect is fabricated with no basis, as al-Suyuti declared. His saying: 'But they established disagreement concerning it' means that the scholars established disagreement concerning the intellect, and there is no place for this parenthetical remark because they also established disagreement concerning the spirit, so perhaps 'but' is for mere emphasis. Then I saw the author in his commentary said: 'But ... etc.' is a parenthetical remark in the manner of those who delve, indicating that they did not agree upon a specific reality, rather they differed in its explanation. End. So the parenthetical remark indicates the spread and abundance of disagreement.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage enumerates three additional types of intellect (third, fourth, fifth) from a longer classification, then discusses the relative merit of intellect and knowledge. The author states that the preponderant view is that knowledge is superior to intellect because knowledge is a divine attribute, while any reports claiming the superiority of intellect are baseless. The passage then comments on a line of the poem that says 'but they established disagreement concerning it,' explaining that this refers to disagreement among scholars about the nature of the intellect. The author notes that this disagreement is extensive, similar to the disagreement about the spirit, and the parenthetical remark serves to highlight the widespread difference of opinion.

عقل شرفي

Misconception: Intellect is only the natural reasoning ability common to all humans.
Correction: The author shows that intellect has special divine forms given to believers and prophets.

Checkpoint

B) The intellect of ascetics

There are divinely granted intellects beyond natural reason—given to believers, ascetics, and the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The fourth intellect is that of the ascetics, enabling zuhd. When you look at your attachment to wealth, status, and comfort, do you see the intellect of zuhd working in you, or are you enslaved to the world? What one possession or habit can you give up this week to prove you are serious?
?
The Prophet's intellect is the most honorable. Do you ever feel that your own intellect is sufficient, or does this truth humble you into seeking knowledge from his example? Will you read a hadith today with the intention of receiving even a fraction of that honorable intellect?

Superiority of Knowledge over Intellect
Argues for the superiority of knowledge over intellect and explains disagreement on intellect's definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the preponderant view that knowledge (especially divine knowledge) is superior to intellect, and why reports favoring intellect are baseless.

Core Idea
Knowledge is greater than intellect because it is a divine attribute.

After listing intellect types, the author addresses a debate: which is better, intellect or knowledge? He settles the matter by declaring that knowledge is superior, as it is an attribute of Allah Himself, and any hadith claiming otherwise is fabricated. He also notes that scholars have disagreed about the definition of intellect itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the superiority debate
Read the Arabic passage from 'وقد اختلف' to 'لا أصل له'. Notice the author's clear preference for knowledge.
2
Understand the reasoning
Knowledge is superior because it is among Allah's attributes; intellect is a created faculty. So knowledge is higher.
3
Address the false reports
The author states that reports claiming intellect is better are fabricated and baseless, citing al-Suyuti.
This refutes any weak hadith on the topic.
4
Examine the disagreement about intellect
The passage then comments on a poem line: 'but they established disagreement concerning it'. This refers to scholars disagreeing on the reality of intellect.
5
Note the parenthetical remark
The author explains that 'but' is for emphasis, showing that disagreement about intellect is widespread, similar to disagreement about the spirit.

The Obligation to Believe in Resurrection: Divine Law Basis
Al-Bajuri states belief in three eschatological matters is wajib sam'an, noting consensus and opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in resurrection is obligatory based on divine law (sam'an) and how this differs from rational obligation.

Core Idea
Resurrection is obligatory to believe because it is possible and reported by the truthful Prophet.

This lesson explores a key passage from al-Bajuri's commentary on the Jawharat al-Tawhid. The author clarifies that the obligation to believe in resurrection, gathering, and reckoning is not based on reason alone but on divine revelation (sam'an). This distinction is crucial for understanding the nature of Islamic creedal obligations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the text's structure
Identify the grammatical structure: 'wājib' is the predicate of 'su'ālanā' and its conjuncts. The three matters are the subject.
The metrical note about sukūn on the bā' is for poetry, not doctrine.
2
Grasp the reasoning for obligation
The passage gives a concise syllogism: every possible matter reported by a truthful person is obligatory to believe; these three matters are possible and reported by the truthful Prophet; therefore they are obligatory.
This is wujūb samʿī, not ʿaqlī.
3
Note the sectarian positions
Ahl al-Sunna and majority Mu'tazila affirm; the Mulhida (atheists) deny all three. Recognize that even the Mu'tazila, despite their rationalism, accept this obligation because it is based on revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (واجب) بسكون الباء للوزن، وهو خبر قوله : (سؤالنا)، وما عطف عليه، فكلُّ واحدٍ من الثلاثة المذكورة واجب سمعاً ؛ لأنه أمر ممكن أخبر به الصادق، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو واجب، وهذا ما عليه أهل السنة وجمهور المعتزلة، وأنكرت الملحدة كُلا هذه الثلاثة .
His saying (wājib) is with a sukūn on the bā' for the meter, and it is the predicate of his saying (su'ālanā) and what is conjoined to it. So each one of the three mentioned is wājib sam'an (obligatory by divine law), because it is a possible matter reported by the truthful one, and everything that is so is wājib. And this is what Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila hold, and the Mulhida (atheists) denied all of these three.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the obligation of believing in three eschatological matters: resurrection, gathering, and recompense. The author explains that the word 'wājib' in the poem is pronounced with a sukūn on the bā' for metrical reasons. This word is the predicate of the subject 'su'ālanā' (our inquiry) and what is conjoined to it. The intended meaning is that each of the three matters—ba'th (resurrection), hashr (gathering), and hisāb (reckoning) or reward/punishment—is wājib sam'an, meaning obligatory to believe because it is a logically possible matter that has been authentically reported by the truthful prophet (the Prophet Muhammad). The author then states the position of the orthodox community: Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila affirm this obligation. In contrast, the Mulhida (those who deny divine law, i.e., atheists or materialists) reject all three.

Key Terms
واجب سمعاً
أهل السنة
المعتزلة
الملحدة
الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the obligation is rational (ʿaqlī) rather than based on revelation.
Correction: The passage explicitly says it is wājib sam'an (by divine law), not ʿaqlan.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is belief in the three eschatological matters considered obligatory?
A) Because they are logically necessary
B) Because they are possible matters reported by the truthful Prophet
C) Because Ahl al-Sunna agreed upon them
D) Because the Mu'tazila accepted them

Key Takeaway
Belief in resurrection is obligatory not because reason demands it, but because divine revelation confirms it as a possible event reported by the truthful Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe in the resurrection as a certain reality that will happen to you personally, or is it merely a distant theological concept? How does your daily life reflect that belief in a way that would be visible to others? What would change if you lived with absolute certainty that you will be resurrected and held accountable?
?
The passage states that the obligation to believe is samʿī, not ʿaqlī. Have you ever relied on your own reasoning to determine what is true in matters of the unseen, rather than submitting to the report of the truthful? In what area of your faith are you most prone to letting your intellect override revelation? What step can you take today to practice taslīm (submission) to a revealed truth that your mind struggles with?

The Indivisible Atom as an Accident and Proof for the World's Temporal Origination
The commentator affirms the atom as an accident and refutes the philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic theological position on the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) as an accident (arad) and its role in proving the temporal origination of the world (huduth al-alam).

Core Idea
The indivisible atom is an accident, not a substance, and its affirmation proves the world is created.

This passage from the commentary on the Tuhfat al-Murid addresses a key cosmological argument in Islamic theology. The commentator affirms the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) as an accident (arad) specifically to refute the philosophers who denied it. Understanding this concept is crucial because it directly impacts the proof for the world's temporal origination (huduth). Let's examine the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Notice the technical terms and the structure of the argument.
Pay attention to the phrase 'عندنا لا ينكر' – it establishes the Muslim stance.
2
Understand the claim: atom as accident
The commentator states that for Muslims, the indivisible atom is an accident, not a substance. This is a key distinction from the philosophers' view. Reflect on why this matters.
An accident (arad) is something that inheres in a substance and is not self-subsistent.
3
Recognize the stakes: world's temporality
The commentator explains that affirming the atom leads to the conclusion that the world is temporally originated, while denying it leads to the philosophers' claim of eternity. This shows the theological importance of the issue.
The connection between atom and huduth is central to Islamic cosmology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عندنا فهي عَرَض لا جوهر وقوله : ( عِنْدَنا لا يُنْكَرُ ) أي : عندنا معاشر المسلمين لا يُنكر ثبوته، وتقرره في الوجود ؛ لأن الله قادر على تفريق الأجسام بحيث لا يبقى جزء على جزء، وغرضه بذلك الرد على الفلاسفة المنكرين للجوهر الفرد، ويترتب على الخلاف في ثبوته وعدمه القول بحدوث العالم ،وقدمه، وإذا علمت ذلك علمت أن هذه المسألة ينبغي معرفتها والاعتناء بها، فتفطّن.
المسألة في المحصل للإمام الرازي ( ص (۸۳) ، والأجسام عند الفلاسفة متصلة غير منفصلة، والصورة عندهم هي التحيز، فالهيولى عندهم هي القابل والاتصال والوحدة هي الصورة، وهذا على رأيهم في نفي الجوهر الفرد، وأما على إثباته فالقابل هو الجوهر، ويعرض له التأليف فيصير جسماً. كذا علق عليه الطوسي.
And as for us, it is an accident not a substance. And his statement: 'With us it is not denied' means: with us, the community of Muslims, its establishment and confirmation in existence is not denied, because God is able to separate bodies such that no part remains on another part. His purpose by that is to refute the philosophers who deny the indivisible atom. And upon the dispute concerning its existence and non-existence depends the statement of the temporality of the world and its eternity. And when you know that, you know that this issue deserves to be known and attended to, so be perceptive. The issue is in al-Muhassal of Imam al-Razi (p. 83): Bodies according to the philosophers are continuous and not discrete, and form according to them is occupation of space (tahayyuz), so matter (hayula) according to them is the receptive [substrate], and continuity and unity are form. This is according to their view in negating the indivisible atom. But according to its affirmation, the receptive is the atom, and composition happens to it so it becomes a body. Thus commented by al-Tusi.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argument. The commentator asserts that the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) is an accident (arad) according to us (Ahl al-Sunna), not a substance. He explains that the poet's line 'With us it is not denied' means Muslims affirm its existence in reality. The proof: God has power to separate bodies so completely that no part remains attached to another—this implies that bodies are composed of indivisible parts. The purpose is to refute philosophers (falasifa) who deny the atom. The significance: the dispute over the atom's existence directly determines whether the world is temporally originated (hadith) or eternal (qadim). The commentator concludes by emphasizing the importance of this issue. The footnote adds that in al-Razi's Muhassal, philosophers view bodies as continuous (not composed of atoms) and define form as spatial occupation; but if the atom is affirmed, the atom itself is the receptive substrate and composition yields a body.

Key Terms
الجوهر الفرد (indivisible atom)
عرض (accident)
حدوث العالم (temporal origination of the world)
الفلاسفة (philosophers)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the indivisible atom is a substance (jawhar) like in Greek atomism.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that for Muslims, the atom is an accident (arad) that inheres in bodies, not a self-subsistent substance.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of affirming the indivisible atom according to the commentator?
A) To prove the philosophers right
B) To establish the foundation for proving the world's temporal origination
C) To deny God's power
D) To support the eternity of the world

Key Takeaway
The indivisible atom is affirmed by Muslims as an accident, and it serves as a proof for the world's temporal origination (huduth).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage argues that affirming the indivisible atom is necessary to affirm that the world had a beginning. Do you truly live as if the world—and you—are created, or do your daily habits betray a sense of self-sufficiency? Identify one moment today where you will consciously remember your contingency and turn to the Creator.
?
The philosophers denied the atom to avoid admitting the world's temporal origination. What subtle resistance do you feel inside when faced with proofs that demand your submission? What part of your life do you still act as though you are independent of Allah? Commit to a specific act of reliance on Him before this day ends.
?
The commentator stresses that this issue 'deserves to be known and attended to.' Are you giving the study of aqeedah the attention it demands, or are you content with superficial understanding? What concrete change will you make this week to deepen your engagement with these foundational truths?

Understanding 'When Asked Absolutely' and 'Our Proof'
Commentator defines two key terms from the poem.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the phrases 'when asked absolutely' and 'our proof' in the context of theological questioning, and how they apply to this world, the grave, and the Hereafter.

Core Idea
The proof in the afterlife is the answer itself, not an external argument.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks two key phrases from the poem. The first clarifies that 'absolute' questioning encompasses all realms. The second explains that 'our proof' is a sound argument, but in the Hereafter, the answer itself suffices as proof. Let's see how these terms are defined and why they matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage includes both the main text and important footnotes.
2
Understand the scope of 'absolute question'
The commentator explains that 'when the question absolutely' means questions in this world, the grave, and the Resurrection. Note the nuance that the principle of preceding/succeeding context is not absolute.
This shows the comprehensiveness of the term.
3
Distinguish the proof in this world vs. the afterlife
The passage defines 'our proof' as a correct legal argument. The footnote clarifies that in the Hereafter, the answer itself is the proof, not a separate evidence. Compare the two contexts.
The Quranic example illustrates how God inspires the proof.
4
Reflect on the Quranic example
The commentator quotes verse 82:6, where the servant is inspired to say that God's generosity deceived him. Consider how this shows the subtlety of God's granting the proof.
This ties the abstract concept to a concrete scriptural reference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (عِنْدَ السُّؤَالِ مُطلَقاً ) أي : عند ورود السؤال علينا من الغير حال كونِ السؤال مطلقاً ؛ أي: في الدنيا وفي القبر وفي القيامة كما يُفهم ذلك من المقام، وإن لم يُفَسِّر الإطلاق هنا سابقٌ ولا لاحق. وقول العلماء الإطلاقُ يُفسِّرُهُ سابق أو لاحق أمرٌ أغلبي، كما قاله بعض المحققين . وقوله : (حُجَّتَنَا ) :أي ما نحتج به على جواب (۱) ذلك السؤال احتجاجاً صحيحاً شرعيًّا، بحيث لا طعن فيه ولا امتناع من قبوله . قال بعضُ العارفين : من لُطْفِ مَنْح الله الحُجَّةَ للإنسان عند السؤال قوله تعالى: أَيُّهَا الْإِنسَنُ مَا غَرَكَ بِرَبِّكَ الكَرِيرِ [الانفطار : ٦]، فإنه ألهمه الحُجَّة بأن يقول : غَرَّني كرمُكَ يا رَبُّ.
(۱) قوله : (أي: ما نحتج به على جواب إلخ ) هذا ظاهر في السؤال الوارد في الدنيا ؛ لأن السائل في الدنيا قد يطلب دليلاً على الجواب، وأما جواب السؤال الوارد في الآخرة فاحتياجه إلى دليل يدل عليه غير ظاهر ؛ لأنه لم يرد أن الملائكة يطلبون من الميت بعد جوابه دليلاً يثبت به جوابه، بل متى وفقه الله ، وأجابهم انصرفوا عنه، وقالوا له : نَم نومة العروس، فكان الظاهر حمل الحجة على نفس الجواب. هذا ما ظهر . انتهى أجهوري.
(۲) قوله : (من لطف) عبارة الأمير من لطيف. انتهى أجهوري.
His saying: 'when the question absolutely' means: when the question comes to us from another while the question is absolute; i.e., in this world, in the grave, and in the Resurrection as understood from the context, even though no preceding or following context here explains the absoluteness. And the scholars' saying that the absoluteness is explained by something preceding or following is a majority matter, as stated by some investigators. And his saying: 'our proof' means: that by which we argue in answer to that question, a correct legal argument, such that there is no criticism of it nor refusal to accept it. Some gnostics said: from the subtlety of God's granting the proof to a person at the time of the question is His saying, Exalted: 'O man, what deceived you concerning your generous Lord?' [al-Infitar 6], for He inspires him with the proof to say: 'Your generosity deceived me, O my Lord.'
Footnote (1): His saying: (i.e., that by which we argue in answer, etc.) This is apparent regarding the question that occurs in this world, because the questioner in this world may ask for evidence of the answer. As for the answer to the question that occurs in the Hereafter, its need for evidence to indicate it is not apparent, because it has not been reported that the angels ask the deceased after his answer for evidence to confirm his answer; rather, when God grants him success and he answers them, they turn away from him and say to him: 'Sleep like the sleep of a bride.' So the apparent meaning is to interpret 'al-hujja' as the answer itself. This is what appears. End of al-Ajhuri.
Footnote (2): His saying: ('min lutf') the expression of al-Amir is 'min latif'. End of al-Ajhuri.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on two phrases from the poem: 'when the question absolutely' and 'our proof'. The commentator first explains that 'when the question absolutely' means the question that comes to us from another in an absolute sense, encompassing this world, the grave, and the Hereafter. He notes that the principle that absoluteness is explained by a preceding or following context is only a general rule, not absolute. Then he explains 'our proof' as a correct legal argument that cannot be criticized or rejected. He mentions a subtle point: God's granting of the proof is seen in the verse 'O man, what deceived you concerning your generous Lord?', where the servant is inspired to answer that it was God's generosity that deceived him. The first footnote further clarifies that the interpretation of 'hujja' as an argument applies primarily to this-worldly questioning; in the Hereafter, the 'hujja' is actually the answer itself, not a separate proof. The second footnote corrects an expression: the word 'lutf' is better read as 'latif' according to al-Amir.

Key Terms
السؤال المطلق (al-suʾāl al-muṭlaq)
الحجة (al-ḥujja)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the proof (hujja) in the afterlife requires explicit external evidence.
Correction: The text clarifies that in the Hereafter, the answer itself serves as the proof, as the angels accept it without further evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what does 'when the question absolutely' ('inda al-suʾāl muṭlaqan) include?
A) Only questions in this world
B) Questions in this world, the grave, and the Day of Resurrection
C) Only questions in the grave
D) Only questions on the Day of Resurrection

Key Takeaway
The absolute question covers all stages of existence, and the proof (hujja) is a sound argument; in the Hereafter, the divinely inspired answer serves as the proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face the question in your grave, what will your answer be? Are you living in a way that ensures that answer will be inspired by God's generosity, or are you relying on your own efforts?
?
The verse 'O man, what deceived you concerning your generous Lord?' implies that every person has an excuse. What is your excuse today? Can you honestly say it is based on God's generosity, or is it rooted in negligence?
?
If your answer in the Hereafter serves as your only proof, does your current life's answer align with what you would want that proof to be? What concrete step can you take today to ensure your answer is one of truth?
